--- Commit Message ---
LU-18808 lnet: allow LNDs to discover metadata via pings

The EFA LND needs to be able to automatically discover remote
EFA NIs GID and manager QP data by first performing a handshake
using LNet pings over TCP. This allows communication over EFA
without relying on large NID support and without needing the GID to
be provided externally.

The metadata for all remote NIs for a particular node are passed
via the LNet ping REPLY packet. Since a node will only send its
own NIs metadata, a handshake must be performed with each node
in a cluster.

We define a new LNet callback lnd_get_nid_metadata to enable
LNet to query the LND for NID related metadata to send
alongside the ping REPLY. Of course, this is implemented by the
EFA LND to transmit the GIDs and manager QP data for local NIs.

Currently, this functionality is not used. The first consumer
will be the EFA LND after it is upstreamed.

Test-Parameters: trivial testlist=sanity-lnet serverversion=2.16

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-03-14 14:00:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

(3 comments)

> Patch Set 1:
> 
> No need to reinvent the wheel. LNet allows sending LND specific info, just not with pings. If I remember correct LNDs can request extra space for send and recv packets to include LND specific info. msg_private is used for this but only the LND knows what inside.

The LNDs themselves have tons of control over the actual contents of the send/recv. They can add as many LND specific fields as they'd like. But this serves a different use case. We are using one LND (ksocklnd) to fetch information of behalf of another LND (kefalnd) - in this case, the GIDs. There isn't a way to do that now.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2025-03-14 14:40:33.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

The reason for my dislike of using ping is that ping is limited by how much can data can send back. If we already have too many peers data gets dropped :-( Implement IPv6 made the amount of peer info coming back even smaller.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-03-14 14:57:31.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

> Patch Set 1:
> 
> The reason for my dislike of using ping is that ping is limited by how much can data can send back. If we already have too many peers data gets dropped :-( Implement IPv6 made the amount of peer info coming back even smaller.

I think that's reasonable. This feature is opt-in though. So only users of EFA need to worry about this. The ping buffer will be untouched for everyone else.

Question: In your patch "LU-17700 lnet: properly calculate ping buffer size", how did you derive LNET_PING_BUFFER_MAX as 3960?

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-03-14 15:02:46.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

> Patch Set 1:
> 
> > Patch Set 1:
> > 
> > The reason for my dislike of using ping is that ping is limited by how much can data can send back. If we already have too many peers data gets dropped :-( Implement IPv6 made the amount of peer info coming back even smaller.
> 
> I think that's reasonable. This feature is opt-in though. So only users of EFA need to worry about this. The ping buffer will be untouched for everyone else.
> 
> Question: In your patch "LU-17700 lnet: properly calculate ping buffer size", how did you derive LNET_PING_BUFFER_MAX as 3960?

Oh, I see. Prevent ko2iblnd from trying to do a self-RDMA. Seems like that should be an LND defined value? i.e. LND largest ping value? ksocklnd could send a lot more data on a ping without issues.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2025-03-16 12:51:10.000000000) ---
Patch Set 3: Code-Review-1

I'm not against landing this in advance of EFA LND, but I definitely have questions and requirements for this patch:
- is there a way for "lctl ping" or "lnetctl ping" to print this extra metadata? Does it just end up being the EFA NID as with peer discovery and they will be printed as normal?
- I don't see any of the code to parse/print EFALND NIDs in libcfs_netstrfns[].  That is a requirement for even routing to such networks, and is a low barrier to upstream, even independent of this patch and full EFA support. 
- what is the compatibility/interoperability of this change with older clients?

It _looks_ like there is a feature flag for this, but I have no way to test if this is working properly, and figuring out that there was a bug in the code long after it landed (and maybe made it into a release) would be problematic.

Firstly, please add Test-Parameters: on this patch to run a basic against an older release to provide basic interop testing:

 Test-Parameters: trivial testlist=runtests,sanity-lnet serverversion=2.15

Secondly, please find some way to exercise this code independently of EFA.  Even after EFA might be upstreamed, it cannot be tested anywhere outside AWS, so this code will continue to be exposed to regressions.  Having a sanity-lnet.sh test that enabled (e.g. via fail_loc) a connection with the LNET_PING_FEAT_METADATA flag (and sent _something_ that could be verified by the test) would go a long way to ensuring that this feature was working properly, and continues to work after it is landed.

Who knows, maybe having socklnd send conns_per_peer, and IB send the fragment count and peer credits would avoid a lot of configuration issues with those networks as well.  It would be great if this extra buffer could be e.g. YAML formatted or similar, so it could hold generic config info, and you would get much more buyin to landing it.

Unfortunately, I don't think that this could help us with IB GUIDs, since o2iblnd depends on TCP for the initial connection, so we aren't ahead of where we are today with IPoIB since it would still be needed.  Maybe we just have the MGS on IP and it can distribute the IB GUID NIDs to all of the clients (via LU-10360)?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2025-03-16 13:10:20.000000000) ---
Patch Set 3:

> Maybe we just have the MGS on IP and it can distribute the
 > IB GUID NIDs to all of the clients (via LU-10360)?

Sigh, that doesn't make sense, since all of the nodes would still need IP to contact the MGS, defeating the whole purpose.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-03-16 17:28:58.000000000) ---
Patch Set 3:

> Patch Set 3: Code-Review-1
> 
> I'm not against landing this in advance of EFA LND, but I definitely have questions and requirements for this patch:
> - is there a way for "lctl ping" or "lnetctl ping" to print this extra metadata? Does it just end up being the EFA NID as with peer discovery and they will be printed as normal?

The metadata is defined per-LND, so each LND would need to have it's own printer method.

> - I don't see any of the code to parse/print EFALND NIDs in libcfs_netstrfns[].  That is a requirement for even routing to such networks, and is a low barrier to upstream, even independent of this patch and full EFA support. 

I can add this is another patch. EFA NIDs look just like IPv4 addresses.

> - what is the compatibility/interoperability of this change with older clients?

We've tested this with 2.10/2.12/2.15 and everything works fine. This patch is a forward-port of code from our 2.15 release. Adding the Test-Parameters is a good idea.

> It _looks_ like there is a feature flag for this, but I have no way to test if this is working properly, and figuring out that there was a bug in the code long after it landed (and maybe made it into a release) would be problematic.
> 
> Firstly, please add Test-Parameters: on this patch to run a basic against an older release to provide basic interop testing:
> 
>  Test-Parameters: trivial testlist=runtests,sanity-lnet serverversion=2.15
> 
> Secondly, please find some way to exercise this code independently of EFA.  Even after EFA might be upstreamed, it cannot be tested anywhere outside AWS, so this code will continue to be exposed to regressions.  Having a sanity-lnet.sh test that enabled (e.g. via fail_loc) a connection with the LNET_PING_FEAT_METADATA flag (and sent _something_ that could be verified by the test) would go a long way to ensuring that this feature was working properly, and continues to work after it is landed.

I could add a dummy metadata callback to lolnd and enable that with a fail_loc. Or I could define something in lustre/kunit/. I don't think a test would be too hard to write.

> Who knows, maybe having socklnd send conns_per_peer, and IB send the fragment count and peer credits would avoid a lot of configuration issues with those networks as well.  It would be great if this extra buffer could be e.g. YAML formatted or similar, so it could hold generic config info, and you would get much more buyin to landing it.
> 
> Unfortunately, I don't think that this could help us with IB GUIDs, since o2iblnd depends on TCP for the initial connection, so we aren't ahead of where we are today with IPoIB since it would still be needed.  Maybe we just have the MGS on IP and it can distribute the IB GUID NIDs to all of the clients (via LU-10360)?

This metadata discovery is dependent on every node having a IPv4 address. Every node on AWS is assigned a private IPv4 address already, so this works well for us. And we don't have IPoIB for EFA - so this is the alternative.

The address format is fairly simple: Suppose you have IPv4 172.43.45.6 and EFA interfaces 1 and 2. The LNET interfaces' addresses would be 172.43.45.6@tcp, 45.6.0.1@efa, and 45.6.0.2@efa. Each node assumes all of it's peers have the same CIDR. So if we saw 76.3.0.5@efa, it'd translate to 172.43.76.3@tcp. After pinging that address, we'd get the EFA GID and we can begin communicating exclusively over EFA.

I don't really think this would help with IB, unless someone has a similar setup i.e. IPv4 addresses but no IPoIB.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-04-09 17:50:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 11:

> Thinking about this more, is it possible that what you saw was the GET that you issued to retrieve the metadata was put in LNet peer discovery queue, then discovery issued its own GET, which could have gone to any interface that LNet knew about for that peer?

That could have been it. It wasn't consistent to reproduce. But every now and then, a "GET metadata" ping would generate more traffic over EFA which would cause more "GET metadata" pings (and eventually lock up the client).

I can try to get more debugging logs once we have the upstream kefalnd prepared. My preference would be to land with LNetGetForce() then push a second patch to try and remove it. And I think I fixed the credit accounting in LNetGetForce().

--- Message (Chris Horn, 2025-04-25 16:02:35.000000000) ---
Patch Set 14:

> Patch Set 11:
> 
> > Thinking about this more, is it possible that what you saw was the GET that you issued to retrieve the metadata was put in LNet peer discovery queue, then discovery issued its own GET, which could have gone to any interface that LNet knew about for that peer?
> 
> That could have been it. It wasn't consistent to reproduce. But every now and then, a "GET metadata" ping would generate more traffic over EFA which would cause more "GET metadata" pings (and eventually lock up the client).

Actually this is not possible. Traffic to the LNET_RESERVED_PORTAL cannot trigger discovery because the discovery traffic itself is on this portal. See lnet_msg_discovery().
